--- Commit Message ---
LU-15259 tests: use existing usernames for setfacl

In SLES15.2 and Ubutntu 20 the "bin" and "daemon" users are not
defined in /etc/passwd, causing setfacl to print a cryptic error:

  setfacl -m u:bin:rw f -- failed
  ~     ? setfacl: Option -m: Invalid argument near character 3

Replace "bin" and "daemon" in ACL tests so they are run with user
and group names that exist on all distros currently being tested.
They can also be specified via ACLUSR1/ACLUSR2 in the test config.

The "permission_xattr" test also needs "nobody" user and group.

Also, the "getfacl" command prints users and groups in numerical
order, so the ACL tests will fail if "daemon" < "bin", or if either
group is higher than the "users" group.  Fix them as needed.

Test-Parameters: trivial testlist=sanity-quota,sanity-sec,pjdfstest
Test-Parameters: testlist=sanity env=ONLY=103-154 clientdistro=el7.9 serverdistro=el7.9
Test-Parameters: testlist=sanity env=ONLY=103-154 clientdistro=el8.6
Test-Parameters: testlist=sanity env=ONLY=103-154,SANITY_EXCEPT=130,HONOR_EXCEPT=y clientdistro=el9.0
Test-Parameters: testlist=sanity env=ONLY=103-154 clientdistro=sles15sp3
Test-Parameters: testlist=sanity env=ONLY=103-154 clientdistro=sles15sp4
Test-Parameters: testlist=sanity env=ONLY=103-154 clientdistro=ubuntu2004

ubuntu20 failed the "permissions" test with:

 uid=2(bin) gid=2(bin) groups=2(bin)
 uid=1(daemon) gid=1(daemon) groups=1(daemon)
 users:x:100:
 Adding user bin to group daemon
 :
 [173] $ setfacl -m g:daemon:r,g:bin:w f -- ok
 [175] $ su bin -- ok
 [176] $ : < f -- failed
 ~          ? f: Permission denied

which I _think_ means that the test _should_ have failed with "permission denied", but didn't.  It still looks like the group membership might be wrong, since user "bin" is in group "daemon", which is likely how it got read permission?

 [106] $ mkdir d -- ok

It looks like the CentOS 7.9 failure is caused by a UID/GID mismatch with the server also:

 centos7# id nobody
 uid=99(nobody) gid=99(nobody) groups=99(nobody)
 centos8# id nobody
 uid=65534(nobody) gid=65534(nobody) groups=65534(nobody)

So it will also need to use sanityusr/sanityusr1/quota_usr, which makes me wonder if they all should?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2022-02-01 18:34:44.000000000) ---

Go ahead. Note there are requirements for the users in the tests that I had to reverse engineer:
- UID ACLBIN < UID ACLDMN
- GID ACLBIN < GID ACLDMN
- ACLDMN in ACLBIN group
- UID ACLGRP > both
- UID ACLNBD > both

My strong preference would be for you to specify those accounts rather than hard coding the ORNL IDs into the script. AFAIK, the quota_usr accounts are not suitable, but feel free to try.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2022-02-02 17:40:58.000000000) ---
Patch Set 23:

My testing looks good except for one thing with sanity 103a test.
I'm seeing 

sanity test_103a: @@@@@@ FAIL: run_acl_subtest 'permissions' failed

[191] $ shopt -s nullglob ; echo e/* -- failed

So its a bash vs dash issue. Ideas on how to fix this?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2022-02-02 20:59:38.000000000) ---
Patch Set 23:

> So its a bash vs dash issue. Ideas on how to fix this?

Run bash? :-)

 > This is due to:
 >
 > [191] $ shopt -s nullglob ; echo e/* -- failed
 >                                       ? 1: shopt: not found                    
 > ~                                     ? e/* 

I _think_ this is testing to see if "echo e/*" can read the directory and expand the list of filenames:

 Pathname Expansion
    If no matching filenames are found, and the shell option 
    nullglob is not enabled, the word is left unchanged.  If
    the nullglob option is set, and no matches are found, the
    word is removed.

 $ mkdir /tmp/e
 $ touch /tmp/e/f{1..10}
 $ echo /tmp/e/*
/tmp/e/f1 /tmp/e/f10 /tmp/e/f2 /tmp/e/f3 /tmp/e/f4 /tmp/e/f5 /tmp/e/f6 /tmp/e/f7 /tmp/e/f8 /tmp/e/f9
 $ chmod a-rx /tmp/e
 $ echo /tmp/e/*
 /tmp/e/*
 $ shopt -s nullglob
 $ echo /tmp/e/*


It might be possible to replace this with "find ." or similar, but then the test needs to depend on the exact error printed by find.  Just removing the "shopt -s nullglob" might be OK, and expect the output to be "e/*" ?  You would need to test this on dash.

> So only Janitor fails. Need to talk to Oleg about his setup

Failure that Janitor cares about is in sanity-sec:
 open: Permission denied
 Initially root ruid:rgid 0:0, euid:egid 0:0
	Groups      0 - root, 
 To switch to effective sanityusr uid:gid 500:501
	Groups    501 - user1, 
 Now root ruid:rgid 0:0, euid:egid 500:501
	Groups    501 - user1, 
 sanity-sec test_55: @@@@@@ FAIL: test_55 failed with 13 

On another Janitor test run without this patch:

 Initially root ruid:rgid 0:0, euid:egid 0:0
	Groups      0 - root, 
 To switch to effective lustreuser uid:gid 500:500
	Groups    500 - lustreuser, 
 Now root ruid:rgid 0:0, euid:egid 500:500
	Groups    500 - lustreuser, 
 File /mnt/lustre/d55.sanity-sec/lustreuser/testdir_groups/file successfully written

So it is probably unhappy because sanityusr has UID != GID?  Maybe test_55 can be changed to use group names instead of numbers for:

                 chown root:$USER0 $DIR/$tdir/$USER0
                 chown $USER0:$USER0 $DIR/$tdir/$USER0/testdir_groups

--- Message (Jian Yu, 2022-08-31 08:08:05.000000000) ---
Patch Set 31:

> looks like this break pjdfstests 100% on my setup trying to add the
 > pjd group. Can somebody please look into why?
 > 
 > oleg308-server: oleg308-server.virtnet: executing add_group 65535
 > pjd_grp1
 > oleg308-server: adding group pjd_grp1:65535
 > pdsh@oleg308-client: oleg308-server: ssh exited with exit code 2

Hi Oleg, this is because 'set -e' is set in pjdfstest.sh.

In add_group(), if '$group_name' doesn't exist, then 'getent group $group_name' will exit with 2:
 # getent group pjd_grp1
 # echo $?
 2

Could you please try the latest patch set 31?
